5d:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Idea 1: \"Isn't this just Monopoly?\""}]}]
5e:["$","p",null,{"children":"Monopoly — or rather, The Landlord's Game from which it descended — was literally designed to teach this lesson. Elizabeth Magie created it in 1903 to demonstrate how property ownership concentrates wealth. The game exists. It's culturally ubiquitous. Why not just use it?"}]
5f:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Idea 2: \"A simple compounding game\""}]}]
60:["$","p",null,{"children":"What if we stripped everything to the core mechanism? A game where early advantages directly increase future income. Roll dice, get resources, buy things that give you more resources. Early luck snowballs into late dominance. Simple, clean, focused."}]
61:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Idea 3: \"Life stages\""}]}]
62:["$","p",null,{"children":"What if we made the real-world parallel explicit? Each round is a decade of life. Your starting position is your birth circumstances — some players are born wealthy, others poor. Same rules, different starting points. Watch inequality emerge across a lifetime."}]
63:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Idea 4: \"The deep simulation\""}]}]
64:["$","p",null,{"children":["What if we went further? Not just showing that inequality compounds, but ",["$","em",null,{"children":"why"}]," systems create it. Players could experience the incentives that lead a ruling class to fund universal literacy but gate higher education. Lobbying mechanics. Policy votes. Social capital versus financial capital. The whole interconnected system."]}]
65:["$","p",null,{"children":["This fourth idea — let's call it ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"The Long Game"}]," — is the most ambitious. It promises to teach not just that inequality exists but why it persists, why those with power rationally act to maintain it. It's intellectually exciting."]}]

68:["$","p",null,{"children":"The natural impulse is synthesis: \"What if we combined the life stages framing with the political mechanics and added property like Monopoly and...\""}]
69:["$","p",null,{"children":"This impulse is almost always wrong."}]
6a:["$","p",null,{"children":"Each mechanic adds cognitive load. Each system requires learning, tracking, deciding. A game that tries to teach five lessons often teaches none — players are so busy managing complexity that they never feel the underlying patterns."}]
6b:["$","p",null,{"children":"More importantly, mechanics can work against each other. If players are focused on political maneuvering, they may not notice the compounding economic dynamics. If they're managing property, they may attribute outcomes to territorial strategy rather than structural advantage."}]
6c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"The framework's purpose:"}]," Instead of combining until something breaks, we derive what the game ",["$","em",null,{"children":"needs"}]," from its experiential goals. Ideas that don't serve those goals get cut — no matter how clever they seem."]}]

6e:["$","p",null,{"children":"Without a framework, game design often looks like this:"}]

a3:["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"archetype-economic-engine","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#archetype-economic-engine","className":"peer","children":"Archetype: Economic Engine"}],["$","svg",null,{"xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}]
a4:["$","p",null,{"children":["All four initial ideas share a structural pattern: resource accumulation with compounding effects. This is the ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"economic engine"}]," archetype — a game where you acquire things that help you acquire more things."]}]
a5:["$","p",null,{"children":"Monopoly adds spatial movement (the board), but analysis reveals this is primarily randomization delivery. Dice determine where you land; you interact with whatever's there. The spatial relationships between properties rarely matter strategically. You can't choose to \"go to Boardwalk\" — you arrive by chance."}]
a6:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Decision:"}]," Unless spatial mechanics carry specific thematic weight (not just randomization), we exclude them. This significantly reduces components, rules complexity, and play time."]}]
a7:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Alternative noted:"}]," A \"life path\" spatial structure — where position represents career track or social mobility — might carry meaning. We'll revisit if derivation calls for it. For now, we proceed with pure economic engine."]}]

a9:["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"part-4-level-1--aesthetic-profile","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#part-4-level-1--aesthetic-profile","className":"peer","children":"Part 4: Level 1 — Aesthetic Profile"}],["$","svg",null,{"xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}]
aa:["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"primary-aesthetic-discovery-revelatory-variant","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#primary-aesthetic-discovery-revelatory-variant","className":"peer","children":"Primary Aesthetic: Discovery (Revelatory Variant)"}],["$","svg",null,{"xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}]
ab:["$","p",null,{"children":"The brief is explicit: players should \"feel\" inequality, not just observe it intellectually. This points to Discovery aesthetic — but a specific variant."}]
ac:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Standard Discovery:"}]," Finding something new. A secret room, a plot twist, a hidden mechanic. \"I didn't know this existed!\""]}]
ad:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Revelatory Discovery:"}]," Understanding something known but unfelt. \"I knew this intellectually, but now I ",["$","em",null,{"children":"understand"}]," it.\" The insight comes not from new information but from experiential comprehension of existing information."]}]
ae:["$","p",null,{"children":["Consider the song \"Common People\" by Pulp. The narrator describes a wealthy woman who wants to experience poverty as aesthetic tourism — \"live like common people.\" The song's insight is that she can never truly understand because she can always \"call her dad\" and escape. She knows about poverty. She doesn't ",["$","em",null,{"children":"feel"}]," it."]}]
af:["$","p",null,{"children":"Our game should make that kind of distanced observation impossible. Players should end up unable to treat inequality as abstraction."}]
b0:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Design implications:"}]}]
b1:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Minimal thematic framing at start. Don't announce \"this is about inequality\" — let the mechanics reveal it."}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Inequality should emerge from apparently fair rules. The discovery is \"the rules were the same but the outcomes weren't.\""}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"The \"aha\" moment should be felt, not explained. Revelation through play, not instruction."}],"\n"]}]
b2:["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"secondary-aesthetic-tension","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#secondary-aesthetic-tension","className":"peer","children":"Secondary Aesthetic: Tension"}],["$","svg",null,{"xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}]
b3:["$","p",null,{"children":"Visceral understanding requires Tension. Players falling behind should feel the walls closing in. The gap should create anxiety, not mere observation."}]
b4:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"But carefully calibrated:"}]," Pure Tension without resolution creates suffering, not learning. db:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Mechanism 2: Threshold access"}],"\nOptions only available above certain wealth levels. Gates that only the wealthy can pass.\n",["$","em",null,{"children":"Example: Can't buy education until you have 8 Wealth."}]]}]
dc:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Mechanism 3: Rule asymmetry"}],"\nRules that technically apply equally but functionally benefit the wealthy.\n",["$","em",null,{"children":"Example: Flat fee of 3 Wealth hurts poor players proportionally more than rich ones."}]]}]
dd:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Mechanism 4: Positional advantage"}],"\nBetter position creates better opportunities. The rich have access the poor don't.\n",["$","em",null,{"children":"Example: Investment opportunities only offered to high-wealth players."}]]}]
de:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Mechanism 5: Social/political capital"}],"\nConnections that convert to material advantage. Power beyond mere wealth.\n",["$","em",null,{"children":"Example: Lobbying to change rules in your favor."}]]}]

177:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Principle 1: Same event, different impact"}]}]
178:["$","p",null,{"children":["Every event should affect wealthy and poor players ",["$","em",null,{"children":"differently"}],", even when rules are identical. A medical emergency costing 5 Wealth is a nuisance to someone with 15 Wealth and devastating to someone with 6 Wealth."]}]
179:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Principle 2: Choice reveals constraint"}]}]
17a:["$","p",null,{"children":"Events should create choices that reveal structural constraint. The wealthy player chooses between good options. The poor player chooses between bad ones."}]
17b:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Principle 3: Real-world resonance"}]}]
17c:["$","p",null,{"children":"Events should evoke recognizable life circumstances: healthcare costs, education opportunities, economic downturns, lucky breaks. The parallel to reality should be unmistakable."}]
17d:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Principle 4: Brief resolution"}]}]
17e:["$","p",null,{"children":"Events shouldn't bog down play. Quick to resolve, clear in effect, minimal debate needed."}]

1fe:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"What happens:"}]}]
1ff:["$","p",null,{"children":"The wealthy player hears their life summarized by someone who struggled: \"They never faced a challenge they couldn't handle. Every opportunity was within reach. They leave their children wealth and security.\""}]
200:["$","p",null,{"children":"The working class player hears their life summarized by someone who succeeded: \"They worked hard every round. They faced the same challenges but couldn't afford the solutions. They leave their children... not much. The same position they started in.\""}]
201:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Why cross-eulogies work:"}]}]
202:["$","p",null,{"children":"Writing your own eulogy invites self-justification. Writing someone else's requires perspective-taking. The wealthy player must articulate the poor player's struggle. The poor player must articulate the wealthy player's ease."}]
203:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Step 3: The Final Question (2-3 minutes)"}]}]
204:["$","p",null,{"children":"After all eulogies are delivered, the facilitator pauses. Then:"}]
205:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","em",null,{"children":"\"One last question. Think honestly before you answer."}]}]
206:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","em",null,{"children":"\"What would you have done differently?\""}]}]
207:["$","p",null,{"children":"Go around the table. Each player answers."}]
208:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"What happens:"}]}]
209:["$","p",null,{"children":"The working class player searches for an answer. \"I could have... maybe if I'd saved in Round 2... but then the medical emergency...\" They trail off. The honest answer is: \"Nothing. I couldn't have changed this.\""}]
20a:["$","p",null,{"children":"The wealthy player searches too. \"I guess I made some mistakes in Round 4, but it didn't really matter...\""}]
20b:["$","p",null,{"children":"The question assumes agency. The experience denied it. The gap between question and answer is the lesson landing."}]
20c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","em",null,{"children":"Allow silence."}]," When someone says \"I don't know\" or \"Drawn a different card at the start\" — that's the moment. Don't fill it with explanation."]}]
20d:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Step 4: The Pivot (Optional — 1-2 minutes)"}]}]
20e:["$","p",null,{"children":"If the group has energy and interest, one more question:"}]
20f:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","em",null,{"children":"\"What would need to change — about the game, not about your play — for your answer to be different?\""}]}]
210:["$","p",null,{"children":["This explicitly invites systemic thinking. \"What would ",["$","em",null,{"children":"I"}]," have done differently?\" becomes \"What would need to be different about ",["$","em",null,{"children":"the rules"}],"?\""]}]
211:["$","p",null,{"children":"The answer is: starting conditions. The rules were identical. The start wasn't."}]
212:["$","p",null,{"children":"This pivot is optional. For some groups, the first question is sufficient. For others, the pivot crystallizes the insight. Facilitator discretion."}]

2ba:["$","p",null,{"children":"Success: Wealthy player has 2+ more Assets than Working Class player by Round 4."}]

2ea:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Cooperative variant:"}]," All players work together against \"the system.\" Would teach different lesson about collective struggle. Changes competitive dynamics to cooperative dynamics. Interesting but different."]}]
2eb:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Digital implementation:"}]," Computer handles calculations, enables hidden information, allows adaptive difficulty. Could reach broader audience but loses physicality and social observation. Different medium, different affordances."]}]
2ec:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Campaign mode:"}]," Multiple sessions building a longer narrative. Characters persist, society evolves, policies change. Rich but requires ongoing commitment. Different temporal architecture entirely."]}]
2ed:["$","p",null,{"children":"These aren't better or worse — they're different designs serving different purposes. The framework helps us choose; it doesn't declare one choice correct."}]

2f1:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Systematic evaluation of candidates."}]," Instead of pursuing each idea until hitting dead ends, we mapped requirements first and evaluated against them. Monopoly's problems were structural, not parametric. The Long Game exceeded our constraints. Simple compounding worked but Life Stages improved on it. We identified this through analysis, not trial and error."]}]
2f2:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Explicit tradeoffs."}]," Life Stages vs. The Long Game isn't \"good vs. bad.\" It's breadth vs. depth, accessibility vs. sophistication, teenagers vs. adults only. The framework made these tradeoffs visible before we invested development time."]}]
2f3:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Efficient derivation."}]," From aesthetic goal (revelatory Discovery) to required dynamics (gradual revelation, visible gap) to mechanical specification (Birth Circumstance cards, compounding Assets) to complete playable design — in a structured sequence, not random exploration."]}]
2f4:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Justified decisions."}]," Every design choice traces back to aesthetic goals:"]}]
2f5:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Why no spatial mechanics? They don't serve the teaching goal."}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Why is Wealth lost each round? To force the rich/poor divide in spending patterns."}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Why cross-eulogies? To force perspective-taking."}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Why that final question? Because the answer reveals the lesson."}],"\n"]}]
2f6:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"A playable game."}]," The chapter produces something real — printable, playable, complete. Theory that doesn't produce games is worthless."]}]

300:["$","ol",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Establish context constraints"}]," (Level 0) — What's fixed before you design?"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Define aesthetic goals and audience"}]," (Level 1) — What experience for whom?"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Derive required dynamics"}]," (Level 2) — What must players do and feel?"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Evaluate candidates against requirements"}]," — Which ideas serve these needs?"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Choose and commit"}]," — Make the tradeoffs explicit; pick one path."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Continue derivation"}]," through remaining levels — Temporal architecture, balance paradigm, mechanics, presentation, parameters."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Validate"}]," — Playtest against measurable hypotheses."]}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}]
301:["$","p",null,{"children":"The framework doesn't replace creativity or iteration. It structures the process so creativity is directed and iteration refines rather than discovers. You arrive at playtesting with a design that's structurally sound, needing parameter tuning rather than architectural rework."}]

303:["$","p",null,{"children":"We started with four ideas. The instinct was to combine them: Monopoly's property + Life Stages' framing + The Long Game's politics + ..."}]
304:["$","p",null,{"children":"This instinct is almost always wrong."}]
305:["$","p",null,{"children":"Each mechanic adds cognitive load. Each system requires learning, tracking, deciding. A game that tries to teach five lessons teaches none."}]
306:["$","p",null,{"children":"The framework's discipline is choosing. Life Stages teaches one lesson clearly. It does not teach everything about inequality. It teaches that structural advantages compound under fair rules. That's enough. That's more than most games achieve."}]
307:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Scope is not ambition's enemy."}]," A focused game that delivers one lesson powerfully serves players better than an ambitious game that delivers five lessons weakly."]}]

30b:["$","p",null,{"children":"We ended with Life Stages: a complete, printable board game that accomplishes this goal within 75 minutes, using only household components, runnable by a facilitator who read the rules that morning."}]
